<review>I was a little disappointed this visit. The food was not up to their usual standard.

Lukewarm Mary's Lemon Chicken Soup. Failed to get our order correct. They did make up for it and not charge for the forgotten item when they brought it. The turkish coffee was not hot and not as strong as normal.

My 10 year old grandson always gets the grilled salmon platter. He even commented that the fish was not very warm and the veggies were soggy.

We drove up from San Jose to go to Coyote Point and to especially have lunch at the Mediterranean.  We will more than likely not be returning. It is difficult finding places my grandsons, who travel extensively,  they find to their liking. I was hoping, after our first visit a month ago, this would be that 'go to' place. <user>116363788318643010750< /user>< Text>
Someone told me that Tuolumne means stone houses in native American language,  I guess Tuolumne Meadows means a meadow with stone houses.

However besides the wood lodge built by sierra club in memory of its member Edward Taylor Parsons, I do not find any stone house.

The Soda Springs and Parson's Lodge are the most famous attractions in the Meadows. There is a 1.5 miles trail connected two attractions together.

Soda Spring is just a bubbling soda spring covered by a wood cabin. Till these days animals still drink from the spring to get minerals supplement. So this is warning sign that people shall not drink the water directly

The Lodge is not open to public. and there is really not much to see. Nearby the Lodge is private residence. Just wonder who still live here, considering the Tiago Road is open only several month a year.

The famous pacific crest trail and John Muir Trail meet in the meadow. Personally, I think the  Tuolumne River is the best part of the Meadows.< /Text>

<user>110753367084927927004<//user><user_name>Bob Thompson<//user_name><date>1612729576944</date><Rate>5</Rate>< review>
Tuolumne Meadows is a gorgeous place, just 6.9 miles from the Tioga Road Yosemite Entrance.

Not far inside Yosemite National Park, after climbing the steep Tioga Pass, you'll notice a massive granite dome, Lembert Dome on your right, which people climb to the top of.  You'll then drive over a bridge that spans the Tuolumne River.  We've parked here, and walked along the sparkling Tuolumne River.  It's definitely worth a stop.

Drive a bit further, and you'll see a store just north of Lembert Dome with a fairly sizable parking lot on the left, where you can buy snacks and drinks, hiking gear, plus any conceivable kind of souvenir- hats, key chains, shirts, post cards, etc.  I once bought a nice Tuolumne Meadows hat here.

Just past the store, you'll notice multitudes of cars parked on both sides of the road, and a vast grassy meadow on the right. You're here!  You can see Lembert Dome, off to the southeast, in the distance.  I've seen lots of deer in the meadow, ground squirrels, and also lots of pretty wildflowers growing along the Tuolumne River.  Be sure and put on some good insect repellant, because the nearer you get to the river, the more ferocious these small black mosquitos get.</review>

<rating>5< /rating>< Text>
Gorgeous Alpine meadow, almost untouched by the tourist masses in the valley.  It‚Äôs a bit of a drive and has almost no facilities, so keep that in mind when visiting.  Weather is cool, even in summer when the valley is roasting.  Pacific Crest Trail comes down near here, so you may encounter hikers at the general store. If you‚Äôre looking for a short hike, a trip to the soda springs is recommended.  The meadow sits over 8,000 feet in elevation and won‚Äôt be open until the snow melts. Ask before you start driving.
Keep in mind that some members of your party may be sensitive to high elevation.  We ended up leaving early due to one person feeling really miserable.</Text>

< Text>
A welcome respite from the hordes in Yosemite Valley. Flee from the other tourists, and explore the backcountry! Spectacular day hikes (Lembert Dome, Cathedral Peak, Lyell Canyon), overnights (Glen Aulin, Upper and Lower Cathedral Lakes) and weekend (Miller Lake) trips in all directions.

Tip for John Muir Trail hikers: permitting from Tuolomne is much easier than Yosemite Valley. Hike northbound to YV (20 miles, all downhill), return to Tuolomne via YARTS bus, then continue southbound to Mt. Whitney.<//Text>

<review>Nestled in the quaint old neighborhoods of south Napa, this park is open and full of green beauty. The mixture of open space and trees along with a great kids play area make this park family friendly and a draw to the entire community.

This summer the city started third Tuesdays in Fuller Park. Every third Tuesday of each month live music was played from a bandstand. The unique green open space drew a large crowd who felt the magic of the music in the fresh air as it sailed through the green trees. The effect was what makes this park magical.</review><pics>None<//pics><Resp>None</Resp>< Gmap_id>
